Current Events Commentary

Japan's Situation Moving Forward 13

Japanese Prime Minister Hamaguchi was assassinated. Speculation about the reasons does not extend beyond three possibilities. First, it was a result of the competition between political parties. Second, it was due to the radicalism of young people's thoughts. Third, it was due to the pressure of economic trends. These three conditions are not unique to Japan, but are shared by countries around the world. None of the countries around the world that share these conditions are unaffected by the political situation, and none are spared from being used as tools by opponents of the government. Today's turmoil and unrest in the political situations of various countries are influenced by these three factors. However, among these three factors, the pain felt by economic trends is the most widespread. Young people are affected by this trend, and their thoughts become more and more radical. Political parties encounter this trend, and their opposition to the government intensifies. Therefore, the country with a poor economy is more likely to drive other kinds of resentment and make the political situation more unstable. The government in this state is able to use its easing measures, taking advantage of the situation and疏解 as the opportunity arises, and the爆发 will be slow. If strict measures are used to suppress and逼迫 it to平, then the爆发 will be sudden. The only difference is that.

The competition between the two parties in Japan has been quite fierce. The accumulation of young people's radical thoughts is increasing day by day. And this economic trend has had a great impact on the livelihood of its people. Therefore, its situation is roughly the same as other countries, but in reality, it is more difficult than other countries. After the assassination of Prime Minister Hamaguchi, it will be more difficult to deal with this kind of mutually牵动 trend, and Foreign Minister Shidehara Kijūrō has risen to bear the brunt.

Receiving Important Domestic Telegrams 14

Page 8

Comprehensive Plan for Transportation and Water Conservancy 15

Submitted by Zhu Jiahua, on a comprehensive plan for national transportation and water conservancy, weighing priorities to realize the resolutions of the Third Plenary Session. The full text is as follows: As noted in the political resolutions of the Third National Congress of our Party, the Congress believes that the economic construction that should be prioritized in the future is transportation and water conservancy. These two are the basic conditions for the development of agriculture and industry. If the country can achieve significant success in these areas, society will be able to release other significant new productive forces. This can be asserted with certainty. The root cause of China's current chaos and poverty lies precisely in this. To save the country from danger, one must start with economic construction. Although the country is riddled with problems, all needing attention, it is necessary to weigh the urgency of different issues and determine priorities. These two areas are truly crucial and cannot be delayed. Unfortunately, soon after the opening of the Third Plenary Session, Feng's rebellion caused military tension, affecting all aspects of governance, and the people's livelihood became increasingly impoverished. Consequently, these two aspects of economic construction were also affected, and progress was delayed. Now, fortunately, the great crisis has been quelled, the military situation has ended, and national unification has finally been achieved. Material construction should be pursued urgently to improve the people's livelihood, enrich their civil rights, and guarantee national independence. Jiahua respectfully presents his humble opinions on promoting the development of transportation and water conservancy as follows. Whether they are appropriate or not is respectfully submitted for public decision.

(1) Transportation Undertakings: Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Teachings. In a conversation with reporters from the "Min Li Bao" on railway planning, he said, "Transportation is the mother of industry, and railways are the mother of transportation. The wealth or poverty of a country can be determined by the number of railways it has, and the happiness or suffering of a locality can be measured by the distance to the nearest railway." This shows the great importance of railways. The adjustment of production to supply consumption, and the pivotal role of manufactured goods in exchange and distribution, all rely on convenient transportation. Therefore, Dr. Sun Yat-sen devoted his life to this endeavor, creating a national railway network plan with all his talent and energy. The grand blueprint is what our Party should strive to realize most earnestly. Now, the relationship between railways and the current national situation is further listed below for reference: (1) The issue of political unification: In the past, warlords occupied territories, forming a situation of separatist rule. Their greatest reliance was on the inconvenience of domestic transportation, which often prevented the central government from exerting its authority effectively. They were able to become powerful figures in remote areas because of transportation barriers, which prevented the central government from suppressing them. If railways are built, the central government can dispatch military forces to arrive quickly, and the warlords will lose their dependence. The implementation of government orders will naturally be unhindered. (2) Border defense issues: Russia's designs on Mongolia, France's intentions towards Guangxi and Yunnan, and Britain's plans for Kangding and Tibet have been brewing for a long time and are becoming increasingly urgent. Recently, with the completion of Russia's Central Asian Railway, Xinjiang and Mongolia are surrounded, almost engulfed. Looking back at our country's borders, doors are wide open everywhere, and we even allow others to build roads in the border areas between Tibet, Yunnan, and Vietnam, letting wolves into the house. The dangerous situation is truly unbearable to speak of. For the present, on the passive side, we must seriously stop the construction of roads across our borders and find ways to recover those already built (such as in Yunnan, Vietnam, the Middle East, and South Manchuria). On the active side, we should build our own roads to facilitate immigration and secure the borders, preventing others from plotting against us. Consolidating the border defense is undoubtedly the most important responsibility of railways. (3) Resolving the food problem: Currently, the domestic population is too large and concentrated in the southeast, where land resources are easily depleted, and the population is growing daily. The deep hidden dangers are already beginning to surface. The northwest, on the other hand, has vast fertile land, sparsely populated, which invites the ambitions of imperialists. To take both into account, immigration to secure the borders and promote land reclamation is the best strategy. To achieve this goal, the establishment of numerous railways is essential. Other benefits, such as cultural education relying on transportation for dissemination to achieve universal access, and people's customs being exchanged to make up for deficiencies and assimilate strengths, leading to improved national character, are secondary matters that need not be elaborated upon. The Second Plenary Session passed a resolution for the Ministry of Railways to prepare a railway construction plan using the Gengzi Indemnity and Customs surplus, and the newly added Xin-Long-Sui Line. Although surveying and construction have been carried out in order, the progress has been somewhat slow due to funding constraints. Moreover, the selection of routes is often biased towards the southeast, a densely populated area, which can only aid economic development. Except for the Guangdong-Guangxi and Hunan-Guangxi lines, national defense has not been taken into account. In the deployment of dense and sparse lines, some are forced by environmental factors, such as the Cangshi Line in the first group, which was added at the suggestion of Yan Xishan. Although the route is not unimportant, it was added only because Yan Xishan proposed it for his own convenience at the time. Moreover, He Chengjun later signed the Cangshi Railway loan agreement with Japanese imperialists, which damaged national sovereignty, which is even more hateful. Therefore, Jiahua believes that in addition to the four groups of routes currently planned by the Ministry of Railways, several border defense lines should be added. For example, the Chengdu-Lhasa and Lhasa-Lajiahui lines should be built to consolidate the Tibetan border; the extension of the Dihua-Yining line and the Dihua-Hotan line should be connected to the Xin-Gan-Sui line to protect Xinjiang; and the Zhangjiakou-Kulun line should be quickly completed and extended to Kyakhta, Tannu Uriankhai, and Khovd to prevent Russia from succeeding in its attempts to sow discord in Mongolia. These are all urgent plans. As for funding, the Ministry of Railways' original plan to use the Gengzi Indemnity and Customs surplus for railway construction is a fundamental national plan and should be given priority. If railways are not built quickly, the country will not be able to achieve prosperity and stability, and all other endeavors will be in vain. Once the railways are completed, the generated profits can be used for other purposes, which is a more balanced approach. However, the national railway network is extensive, and although the Gengzi Indemnity and Customs surplus are the foundation, the amount is limited. If we wait for it to accumulate, the process will be lengthy and time will be lost. The railway undertakings of other powers are progressing rapidly, so how can we afford to wait? Furthermore, the Ministry of Railways' original plan was to use these funds only to build the four groups of routes it had planned, which was barely sufficient. If the routes are extended, the funds will naturally be insufficient. After studying Dr. Sun Yat-sen's "The International Development of China," and the article "How to Develop China's Industry," we know that borrowing foreign capital and using foreign talent, while using our own plans to develop China's industry, is originally a beneficial endeavor. To expedite railway construction so that the national economy and people's livelihood can improve daily, it is necessary to absorb foreign capital as much as possible, which should be easily accomplished. As for national defense railways, the economic benefits may not be immediately apparent, and foreigners may be unwilling to invest. Therefore, a long-term strategy must be devised. In short, border affairs are becoming increasingly urgent and cannot be delayed. To secure the borders, the construction of border defense railways must be expedited. The people's livelihood is becoming increasingly impoverished, and to remedy this, the economic lines related to the southeast, southwest, and northwest must be completed quickly. As for fundraising methods, foreign capital must be absorbed for economic railways, and construction should proceed according to our own plans. For national defense railways that are not easily built with foreign capital, other effective strategies must be devised. The important thing is to take action immediately and not hesitate.

(2) Water Conservancy: Today, the severity of floods in China is almost as great as that of war. The provinces in the lower reaches of the Yellow River in North China suffer from floods, while the provinces in the upper reaches suffer from droughts. The areas around the Yangtze and Huai Rivers are also plagued by disasters every year. The provinces of Hunan, Hubei, Jiangsu, and Anhui invariably report floods annually. Therefore, both proactive and reactive water conservancy measures must be planned quickly. According to the three items of transportation development in Dr. Sun Yat-sen's "The International Development of China," a comprehensive plan for domestic waterways is truly magnificent, but it cannot be achieved overnight. As for the waterways that are most urgent and in need of management, the five rivers in North China, the Huai River in Jiangsu and Anhui, the lakes in Hunan and Hubei, and the floods in the West River and North River in Lingnan are particularly pressing. Plans for dredging and guiding water flow cannot be delayed. Attention has been paid to this for more than a day, but little success has been achieved because the water management agencies are fragmented, with numerous branches, making it difficult to achieve results. Although the nature of water varies from place to place and cannot be governed by a single method, it is essential to have a comprehensive plan that considers the overall situation and details the circumstances, so as to gradually implement it effectively. If local authorities act independently, treating the head when it hurts and the foot when it hurts, it will only become more chaotic. The result is that one wrong move can hinder the entire plan, undo all previous efforts, and, even worse, cause harm to our people. This is a great concern. Therefore, for the present, it is necessary to unify the administrative system and establish a supreme agency at the central level to control all national water conservancy affairs. All superfluous branches should be abolished to centralize authority and reduce waste. Then, leading foreign water conservancy experts should be hired as the backbone, assisted by domestic professionals. An investigation team should be organized, utilizing the existing experience of others to assist our country's talent. This team should be made responsible for conducting thorough and detailed investigations within a certain period of time on the most severely affected river systems in the country, regarding their geological, hydrological, climatic, and forest conditions. An accurate and precise plan should be formulated, weighing the urgency and importance, and separating the steps of addressing symptoms and addressing root causes. The plan should be gradually completed with full effort. As for water management funds, they are always extremely scarce. For example, according to the report of the North China Water Conservancy Commission, there was an original comprehensive plan, but the lack of funds forced them to retreat to treating the symptoms. In fact, the cost of treating the symptoms for ten years would have been sufficient to address the root causes, with something left over. However, due to the talk of treating the symptoms, superfluous branches emerged, public funds were wasted, and no progress was made. The expenditure was in vain, even to the point where everyone insisted on their own opinion and acted independently, making the situation increasingly chaotic. If superfluous branches are cut back and a unified system is planned, not only can much of the existing administrative expenses be saved, but also the national situation of financial surpluses and deficits can be assessed as a whole. A well-considered and balanced allocation will naturally be easier and avoid wasteful spending. Moreover, with precise investigation, the design will be complete and meticulous, saving funds. Talent will be concentrated, and opportunities can be assessed for timely deployment without the problem of idleness in one place and busyness in another. Surpluses and deficits can be balanced, saving resources and achieving success. Now that national unification has been successfully celebrated, these wealth-generating undertakings can absorb foreign capital under unified management to advance progress. The path may seem distant, but the results will be near. Careful consideration should be given to seeking long-term stability, which is the responsibility that our Party must bear in leading our people.

Proposal for Developing Agriculture 16

Submitted to the Fourth Plenary Session by the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining, a proposal for developing agriculture by implementing military and industrial model farming and land reclamation, with 450,000 mu of reclaimable wasteland in the Northeast, including Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, the northwest, and Rehe, and 1,242,000 mu of reclaimable wasteland in the Northwest, including Chahar, Rehe, Qinghai, and Xinjiang. Ten thousand soldiers should be selected from the demobilized soldiers and sent to the Northeast and Northwest to carry out land reclamation as a model. After one year, civilian reclamation should be carried out in parallel. The method is to establish two land reclamation bureaus in the Northeast and Northwest, each with five sections: administrative affairs, investigation, engineering, immigration, and agricultural affairs. The land reclamation area should be delineated, with each district accommodating 50,000 people in the first phase. Each soldier will occupy 50 mu of land. The estimated cost is over 30,048,000 yuan, and 30 million yuan should be allocated from the demobilization expenses in three installments, to be received successively by the National Bank of China. It was also proposed to allocate funds for geological surveys to complete the initial construction plan for agriculture and mining.

Proposal for Rectifying Officialdom 17

Submitted by He Chengjun, the proposal for rectifying officialdom is as follows: "I believe that human existence is essential for governance to thrive, and mere laws cannot implement themselves. Governance by people and governance by law cannot be neglected. Recently, the military affairs have come to an end, and the era of political tutelage has begun. Various constructions have intricate plans. If we want to achieve a bright and clear political system, it cannot be done by the effort of one hand and one foot. Therefore, rectifying officialdom is currently a crucial plan. I respectfully list my humble opinions below: (1) Punish corrupt officials severely. Currently, there are many public officials who are honest and self-disciplined, but there are also many corrupt individuals everywhere. Some collude with criminals and manipulate things from top to bottom, while others oppress the good and weak, extorting in various ways, or embezzle public funds to fill their private pockets. Their actions are unscrupulous, and the prevailing atmosphere is destroying the national principles. Compared to the late Qing dynasty and the warlord era, it is even worse. The failure of a country is due to corrupt officials, and the loss of virtue by officials is due to bribery. In the future, once corrupt officials are reported, personnel should be dispatched to conduct a serious investigation. If there is solid evidence, they should be severely punished, and the giver and receiver should be treated equally. If the personnel dispatched to investigate support or conceal the truth, their crimes should be the same. A heavy penalty should be used to govern a chaotic country, as this is the only way to show deterrence and purify the officialdom. (2) Determine the qualifications of public officials. The competence of public officials is related to the quality of officialdom. Therefore, the appointment of public officials must strictly examine their qualifications to prevent mediocrity. Currently, the Ministry of Personnel of the Examination Yuan has established regulations for examining the qualifications of public officials, and the National Government should order their strict implementation. Those who are not currently public officials but have the qualifications of public officials should also be screened and recorded first, pending appointment. Preparations should also be made to conduct various examinations to ensure that no talented people are left out. The appointment of public officials should be limited to those with qualifications, so that those who have not obtained these qualifications can avoid undue aspirations and eliminate the bad habit of competition. (3) Prohibit military officers from interfering in administration. Previously, during the military period, or wherever the military went, administrative officials were appointed, which was a temporary expedient. Or, matters related to administration were handled by military agencies beyond their authority, or administrative agencies occasionally received letters of recommendation from military officers, all of which were unavoidable due to the circumstances. This not only disrupted the administrative system but also made it difficult for military personnel, who were not familiar with administrative affairs, to achieve success. Now that we are working hard on political tutelage, we should select specialized talents for various constructions and use their strengths to achieve twice the result with half the effort. Military officers should not interfere in any way, lest they become an obstacle to the reform of politics. (4)

Promulgate safeguard regulations. Political tutelage and construction depend on collective efforts and striving for success, which cannot be achieved in the short term. Safeguard regulations should be clearly defined for officials at all levels, and those who can fulfill their duties should be allowed to stay in their positions for a long time and should not be easily replaced, so as to encourage progress. Once their positions are secure, the habits of pursuing personal gain and corruption can be eliminated. (5) Promulgate reward and punishment regulations. Reward and punishment regulations should be clearly defined for officials at all levels, and their performance should be evaluated regularly. Those who have made contributions should be rewarded, and those who have made mistakes should be punished, so that those who are diligent, cautious, and honest will be encouraged, and those who are negligent, derelict, and corrupt will be deterred. Once rewards and punishments are clear, everyone will strive to improve themselves, and everything will be accomplished. (6) Stipulate promotion procedures. The selection of officials at all levels should be based on strict examination of qualifications, and their promotion should be based on performance and follow the proper order. Except for those with special talents who should be promoted exceptionally, all others should not be promoted beyond their grade, so as to eliminate the bad habit of seeking advancement through luck. (7) Pay officials generous salaries. Since the rise of the revolutionary army, the central and local governments have called for the construction of a clean government, but some officials at all levels are still corrupt. This is due to bad habits, disregard for laws and regulations, unfair selection, and lax evaluation, but meager salaries are also a factor. Rewarding scholars generously is an ancient teaching. It seems appropriate to revise the salary standards and pay generous salaries to help cultivate integrity. The above seven points are all key points for rectifying officialdom, and for fundamentally addressing the issue, it is important to have the right leadership. The National Government should be instructed to carefully select high-ranking officials to set an example. Whether this is appropriate or not is respectfully submitted for public decision."

Proposal for Prospering Beiping 18

Submitted by He Chengjun, the proposal for prospering Beiping to strengthen national defense, the original text says: "I have observed that Beiping controls the northern passes, connects to the Central Plains in the south, has a majestic terrain, and has been known as an important town since the Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties and the early Republic of China, when it was successively established as the capital. Over hundreds of years of management and construction, all aspects of culture and material have gradually become magnificent. In recent years, due to the success of our Party's revolution and the relocation of the capital to the south, the area has suddenly declined. Chengjun, as the former head of the Beiping Pacification Headquarters, witnessed the desolate scene and carefully observed it during his spare time, thinking about ways to prosper it. I believe that in terms of terrain, products, and transportation, it is possible to find a way to prosper the area. In terms of national defense, people's livelihood, and culture, it is even more necessary to find a way to prosper the area. Now, based on what I have observed, I propose the following plan:

(1) Promote it as the center of northern industry. According to modern major industries, the most important are the copper and iron industries and the fiber industry. The Beiping area has the Longyan Iron Mine and the Kailuan Liugou, Dongxizhaidang, and other major coal mines. All the elements for ironmaking and steelmaking are available. It is also a rich cotton-producing area in the interior and controls the transportation hub of Manchuria and Mongolia to the exterior. It is suitable for operating cotton weaving factories and easily collects raw materials for woolen fabrics. Moreover, there are numerous universities and a concentration of talent, which facilitates research and improvement. Railways intersect, and merchants converge, making transportation convenient. The price of land and labor are also low, making it a natural center for northern industry. The government should allocate large funds to restore the Longyan Iron Mine, so that the Shijingshan Steel Plant in western Beiping can smelt steel, accommodate the unemployed workers in the Beiping area, and supply the backbone for various constructions (each road purchases about 20,000 to 30,000 tons of train wheels from foreign countries every year). On the other hand, large-scale wool and leather factories and textile factories should be established, using the Ping-Sui and Bei-Ning railways to collect wool and leather from Chahar, Suiyuan, Gansu, Ningxia, and the three northeastern provinces, and using the Ping-Han, Ping-Pu, Zheng-Tai, and Cang-Shi railways, as well as the extensive automobile roads, to collect cotton from Shandong, Henan, Shanxi, Hebei, and other places. Imitate the production of felt, woolen cloth, yarn, cloth, and leather products for civilian use to reduce trade deficit. If these two areas are fully developed and operated for many years, the key points will be established, and entrepreneurship will flourish. No land will be wasted, and no one will be unemployed. What is now seen as a desolate and abandoned capital will soon become a prosperous market again. (2) Maintain it as the cultural center of the country. Beiping has been the capital for hundreds of years, and its cultural undertakings have always been the best in the country. In modern times, it has become even more complete. In terms of education, there are the National Peking University, Normal University, Peking University's agricultural, engineering, medical, and art colleges, as well as the Palace Museum and the History Museum, which provide resources for scholars' research. In terms of art, there are magnificent palaces, temples, and mausoleums, which can be viewed by society, and the historical sites are the best in the world. Almost every grass and tree can represent our country's thousands of years of culture. In recent years, with the relocation of the capital to the south, all facilities have gradually declined. The government should recognize the area as the cultural center of the country and allocate funds specifically for the development of culture on a monthly basis, to maintain its existing facilities, further improve and expand them, and become an academic center and a gathering place for arts. Scholars will gather, tourists will yearn, and music will be revived, making it easy to restore the old appearance. (3) Designate Beiping as a military training area. Our country's national defense focuses on the Northeast and Northwest, and peacetime military training and defense should focus on these two areas. Beiping has a magnificent terrain, connecting to Liaodong to the east and controlling Mongolia and Xinjiang to the north. It is the general hub of border defense. Now that the military center has moved south with the capital, the ambitions of Japan and Russia are even more urgent than in the past. The government should designate Beiping as a military training area and relocate the most important military training institutions to the area. Heavy troops should be stationed in the various gardens, utilizing the heroic spirit of Yan and Zhao and training the brave men of Qi and Lu. In the event of a border crisis, it will be convenient to quickly mobilize troops. Even in peacetime, the use of its huge military expenditure and the large consumption of food can increase the vitality of the Beiping market. As for the past prosperity of Beiping, it was due to the gathering of citizens from all over the country. Since the government moved south and all deployments were withdrawn, the situation has plummeted. Now, if it is designated as a military training area, the establishment of various agencies directly and indirectly related to military training, as well as the residence of military officers and their families, will lead to a sharp increase in population and vitality. Although it may not immediately reach the prosperity of the past, it is also a way to gradually prosper. The above three items are very mediocre, but because Beiping is located in an important area and should not be allowed to decline, and because industry, culture, and military training are related to the foundation of the country, I have specifically planned them. Whether they are appropriate or not is respectfully submitted for public decision."

Longjingcun Incident Resolved 19

(Jilin) The Longjingcun incident was resolved after thirteen rounds of negotiations. We paid 10,000 Japanese yen as compensation for the Japanese police officer killed, and the guarantee item was withdrawn by the Japanese. The incident is fully resolved. (Special Dispatch, 15th)

Diplomatic Hotel Banquet 20

Discussions on Internal and External Debt Consolidation

(Nanjing) Wang Zhengting held a banquet at the Diplomatic Hotel on the afternoon of the 15th. Foreign guests included American Ambassador Johnson, Japanese Ambassador Shigemitsu, and the British Counselor. Chinese guests included Zhang Xueliang, Wang Chonghui, Sun Ke, Song Ziwen, and Wang Boqun. During the banquet, informal discussions were held on the issue of consolidating internal and external debt. A group photo was taken together. After the banquet, Sun Ke accompanied Zhang Xueliang to visit the Ministry of Railways. (Special Dispatch, 15th)

(Nanjing) Regarding the issue of consolidating internal and external debt, the government is actively planning to obtain a plan that is considered fair by both creditors and debtors to resolve various legitimately signed debts. It is hoped that the discussions will be smooth and that a result will be achieved soon. However, this matter is of great importance, and no matter what plan is proposed, it must be formally approved by the National Government before it can be formally resolved. (Special Dispatch, 15th)

(Nanjing) The Debt Consolidation Conference was held at Minister Wang's residence at 12:30 PM today. The Chinese side was attended by Chairman Wang Chonghui, Commissioners Song Ziwen, Wang Zhengting, Sun Ke, Kong Xiangxi, and Zhang Xueliang. The participating countries included representatives from Japan, Britain, the United States, France, Italy, Belgium, and the Netherlands, totaling thirteen people. The Japanese participants included Chargé d'Affaires Shigemitsu, Commercial Officer Yokogyou, and Secretary Horiuchi. The meeting began at 2:20 PM after lunch. Chairman Wang Chonghui delivered a speech on behalf of the National Government, stating that the Central Government intends to consolidate the unsecured and uncertain debts among the internal and external debts as soon as possible, and is willing to engage in concrete negotiations with the relevant countries. He hoped that they would cooperate sincerely to achieve the goal of consolidation. Subsequently, a list of Chinese internal and external debts and the National Government's consolidation plan were distributed to the representatives of various countries, who expressed their understanding. The meeting adjourned at 3:30 PM. The next meeting will be held after the countries study the original plan and incorporate the representatives of the Chinese creditor groups. The venue and date are yet to be determined. (Telegraphic Dispatch, 15th)

Jiangxi People Appeal Regarding Communist Calamities 30

(Nanjing) Liu Zuozhou and other executive members of the Jiangxi Provincial Party Headquarters came to Beijing and, together with the Jiangxi Fellow-Provincials Association, presented to the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee and the National Government a statement of the crimes of the communists: 1. Burning contracts and dividing land; 2. Raping women regardless of age and sharing wives; 3. Killing methods included cutting open stomachs and digging out intestines, or cutting piece by piece, or chopping off hands and feet; 4. Kidnapping for ransom; 5. Confiscating farmers' grain and merchants' goods; 6. Except for hooligans and local thugs, all were labeled as local tyrants and evil gentry. More than 149,900 people have been brutally murdered by the bandits in the province, property losses amounted to more than 320 million yuan, more than 103,000 houses were burned, and about 1.4 million people fled. Of the 81 counties in the province, 37 are completely communist-controlled, and 38 are half communist-controlled. The goals of the appeal are: 1. Order the military authorities to eliminate all communist bandits in the province within a time limit; 2. The National Government should bear all expenses for suppressing the bandits; 3. Quickly allocate large sums of money to relieve millions of refugees; 4. Use the power to overthrow warlords to eliminate the communist bandits. (15th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Five representatives from Jiangxi Province in Shanghai – Wu Nanpu, Zeng Yuchen, He Rufei, Qian Pinsong, and Rao Junqi – arrived in Beijing from Shanghai this morning. They will immediately join forces with petitioning representatives from various parts of Jiangxi Province in Beijing to petition the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, appealing to Commander-in-Chief Chiang to move his headquarters to Jiangxi to oversee the suppression of the communist bandits, and to quickly allocate funds to relieve the victims of the disaster. (15th Dispatch)

Party Affairs Workers Will Not Be Hired Through Examinations 31

(Nanjing) The Beijing Municipal Party Headquarters previously submitted a request to the Central Executive Committee, ordering all levels of party headquarters to implement an examination system for the employment of party affairs workers in the future. Now, the instruction received states that party affairs workers and political workers are fundamentally different in nature. Party members who serve in the party should, by their nature, absolutely embrace the determination to sacrifice for the people. Therefore, the essence of their service cannot be equated with political power, nor can it be equated with administrative power. The Regulations for the Appointment of Party Affairs Workers already have provisions in Articles 3 and 4, which severely restrict the qualifications for the appointment of party members, and the registration itself has a testing effect, which is more detailed than ordinary examinations. The request should be rejected. (15th Dispatch)

Wang Hanming's Troops Complete Muster 35

Foreign Important Telegrams

Japanese Foreign Minister Shidehara Concurrently Serves as Acting Prime Minister 74

HamaGuchi's Condition is Good, Maruyama, the Police Chief, Takes Responsibility and Resigns

The Young Assassin's Actions Stemmed from Patriotic Beliefs

▲United Press of Japan, Tokyo, 15th Dispatch: Today's special cabinet meeting decided, in accordance with Article 8 of the Cabinet Organizational Law, to have Foreign Minister Shidehara concurrently serve as Acting Prime Minister.

▲United Press of Japan, Tokyo, 15th Dispatch: At 2:00 pm on the 15th, Dr. Shiota reported Prime Minister Hamaguchi's condition as follows: From yesterday to this morning, 1,000 grams of Ringer's solution has been injected to maintain his strength, so Hamaguchi's vitality is still strong. According to the current situation, there is no danger of developing peritonitis. If he can hold on until tomorrow, it can be determined that there is absolutely no chance of developing peritonitis. Tonight, after fully adjusting the intestinal junction, he may need to drink tea. A sleeping pill will be injected tonight to help him sleep. No gas has leaked.

▲United Press of Japan, Tokyo, 15th Dispatch: At 3:30 pm on the 15th, Prime Minister Hamaguchi's condition was as follows: temperature 37.4 degrees, pulse 92, respiration 15, no abdominal pain, progress is good. Also, at 6:00 pm, the condition was: temperature 37.8 degrees, pulse 106, respiration 19, the fever is slightly higher than in the morning, and the pulse has also increased. When stroking the abdominal wet cloth, the abdominal wall felt soft, but there was no pain, only a slight discomfort in the stomach.

▲Dentsu, Tokyo, 15th Dispatch: Dr. Shiota visited Prime Minister Hamaguchi's condition at 7:00 pm and told reporters that the Prime Minister's condition was not much different from noon. When asked if he had abdominal pain, he replied that it was not very painful. He also said that Hara Takashi (former Prime Minister) and I were both assassinated, and the Tokyo station chief must feel troubled. Thirty hours have passed since the injury, and peritonitis should not occur again, but at this moment it is still difficult to say that it will not occur. If there are no changes tonight, there should be no worries tomorrow, he said.

▲United Press of Japan, Tokyo, 15th Dispatch: Dr. Shiota performed the surgery on Prime Minister Hamaguchi's wound at 0:15 pm on the 14th. The Prime Minister was lying on the operating table, and because local anesthesia was used, he was conscious and his face showed signs of pain from time to time. Dr. Shiota, wearing a pure white surgical gown, began the operation at 0:37 pm. The doctor immediately discovered the marks where the bullet had penetrated, cut off part of the intestine, and examined it in detail. Dr. Shiota continued to operate and found the bullet in the hip joint, but it could not be removed at present and it was decided to leave it in place for the time being. At 2:00 pm, the wound was sutured and the surgery was completed.

▲Dentsu, Tokyo, 15th Dispatch: At 2:00 pm today, Police Chief Maruyama visited Interior Minister Adachi at his official residence and formally submitted his resignation, taking responsibility for the Prime Minister's assassination. Adachi tried to persuade him to stay, but Maruyama was determined to leave.

▲Reuters, Tokyo, 15th Dispatch: Police authorities still do not want to disclose any information about the interrogation of the assassin who attacked Prime Minister Hamaguchi. However, the main reason for the assassination, the opposition to the London Naval Treaty, has gradually become clear. The assassin is similar to the one who assassinated Prime Minister Hara Takashi nine years ago, a frivolous youth who believes that assassinating the Prime Minister is a patriotic act. Japanese public opinion, including the Prime Minister's political enemies, is indignant about this. Major newspapers are wringing their hands, saying that this is a common occurrence in Japan, calling it a disgrace to a constitutional country, regardless of its purpose.

Army War Preparedness Issues 75

German Representative's Proposal for Direct Restrictions Was Vetoed, China's Representative Abstained

▲National News Agency, Geneva, 14th Dispatch: Germany's motion to include provisions for directly restricting army war materiel in the Disarmament Convention was vetoed in the Disarmament Preparatory Committee today by a vote of nine to nine. The United States, Canada, the Netherlands, Sweden, the Soviet Union, Italy, Turkey, and Venezuela all supported the motion. France, Belgium, Japan, Finland, Poland, Persia, Romania, Czechoslovakia, and Yugoslavia all opposed it. China, Britain, Bulgaria, Spain, Ireland, and Norway all abstained from voting. Similar motions proposed by the Soviet Union and Italy suffered the same fate. Therefore, the principle of direct restriction has been definitely shelved. As for Britain's motion for indirect restrictions within the budget, it was passed with 16 votes in favor, with only Germany, Italy, and the Soviet Union against it. The remaining six representatives abstained from voting. Later, Chairman Loudon announced the news of the assassination of Japanese Prime Minister Hamaguchi and conveyed his condolences and wishes to Japanese representative Sato, expressing hope for the Prime Minister's recovery. The meeting was then adjourned until next week.

Mexican Currency Plummets 76

Difference Between Gold and Silver Currency is 15 Percent

▲Reuters, New York, 14th Dispatch: News from Mexico City, the Mexican currency has plummeted, and the banking and business circles there are quite anxious. They are currently consulting with government officials in order to prevent a crisis. The silver Mexican peso is 15 percent lower than the gold Mexican peso. Usually, the difference between the two currencies is only 3 percent. The US dollar value of both Mexican gold and silver coins has fallen. Today, 259 silver Mexican pesos or 224 gold Mexican pesos are equivalent to 100 US dollars. Many commercial firms are now reducing their business operations to wait for the development of the silver market. The Mexican government has recently withdrawn 10 million silver pesos in order to increase the exchange rate of silver against gold, but this and other equally positive methods have had no significant effect.

Polish Parliamentary Re-election 77

The Government and Opposition Parties' Situations: Roughly Speaking, the Central Left Wing Alliance Announces its Political Program

Pilsudski Will Continue to Hold Power

▲ Warsaw Dispatch: Poland's fourth parliamentary general election since its restoration has been set for November 16th. A total of 444 members of the lower house will be directly and secretly elected on that day, with equal voting rights for men and women without discrimination. As for the 111 members of the upper house, they will be elected on the 23rd of the month. In reality, this so-called general election is merely a test of the Polish people's trust in or distrust of their dictator, General Pilsudski. It is expected that after the election, Poland's major policies will still be controlled by Pilsudski. Even if the election is lost, he is determined not to give up the power he has gained. His intention is that if Poland wants to become a strong country, it must reform its constitution so as to create a strong and permanent new government that is not affected by the changing trends of the parliament. In this election, Pilsudski himself is also one of the candidates, with his name listed in both the upper and lower houses. As a result, the ruling party has greatly increased its power. Pilsudski has now organized a "non-party union" to cooperate with the government, which includes representatives from all three levels, upper, middle and lower, who do not belong to any political party, ranging from large landlords and industrialists to farmers and merchants. It is able to provide a lot of help to the government. As for the anti-government parties, they occupied a majority in the last parliament, but since being dissolved by Pilsudski, they have not been very united. The largest opposition force is the so-called "Union for the Protection of People's Rights and Freedoms," formed by the Polish Socialist Party, the National Labor Party, and three other peasant parties. Originally, the union consisted of five parties, but the Christian Democratic Party recently withdrew, leaving only four parties, referred to as the Central Left Wing Alliance. Many of its important leaders have been arrested and imprisoned by Pilsudski, but its power is still expected to be considerable in this election. In addition, the far-right National Democratic Party is also strongly opposed to the government. The party's policies fundamentally conflict with those of Pilsudski. Since the revolution of 1926, its power has greatly decreased, but recently there have been signs of revival. When the last parliament was dissolved, there were a total of 16 political parties, but in this election, the number of parties has decreased by about one-third due to the merger of various parties. The Central Left Wing Alliance recently issued a declaration, announcing its political program, which mainly includes relief for unemployment, support for economic recovery, improvement of the tax system, reduction of national expenditures, and at the same time, the organization of a sound government based on the people's faith and support, eliminating the dictatorial system. As the election day approaches, Pilsudski's high-handed measures are becoming more and more severe. Many of Pilsudski's current political enemies were once his close friends. According to general observers, in the future new parliament, the various opposition parties may jointly propose a motion of no confidence in the government, but even if it is proposed, the national situation may not change, because Pilsudski's power does not come from the parliament, but from the result of the three days and nights of fighting in Warsaw. As for the future of the election, it is also very chaotic. A certain famous conservative newspaper predicts that this election is like a blind man seeking the way, because very few Polish people are educated, especially in the former Russian territory, where residents lack knowledge and are incited by the Soviet Union, and the public sentiment is gradually becoming radical, which has a greater impact on the poor people without property. Therefore, the election result is still unpredictable, but one point to note is that Germany has recently been making great efforts to revise the border movement. If it becomes a reality, it will endanger Poland's security, causing the Polish people to be very nervous. The whole country is unanimously inclined to resist Germany. Therefore, at least on this point, the parliament and the government may have a kind of understanding, in order to seek diplomatic success. (World)
